# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-kafka-sec-001: Kafka SASL Authentication Flow Security Analysis

## Task

Trace the Apache Kafka SASL authentication flow from channel creation through mechanism negotiation (PLAIN, SCRAM-SHA-256, OAUTHBEARER, GSSAPI), the challenge-response exchange, principal extraction, to ACL-based authorization. Identify all entry points where untrusted client data enters the SASL subsystem, map the data flow through each authentication mechanism, and analyze the security properties of the authentication and authorization chain.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 (mirror of apache/kafka) (Java, ~1.2M LOC)
- **Category**: Security Analysis
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/` (authenticator, plain, scram, oauthbearer packages) and `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/` (channel builders)

## Requirements

1. Identify all entry points where untrusted data enters the SASL subsystem (client connections, SASL tokens, handshake requests)
2. Trace the channel builder architecture: how `ChannelBuilders` creates `SaslChannelBuilder` which wires up `SaslServerAuthenticator`
3. Map the SASL handshake protocol: `ApiVersionsRequest` -> `SaslHandshakeRequest` -> mechanism-specific exchange -> authenticated principal
4. Trace at least two mechanism implementations (PLAIN and SCRAM) through their callback handlers to credential verification
5. Identify how `KafkaPrincipal` is extracted post-authentication and how `Authorizer.authorize()` enforces ACLs
6. Document existing mitigations and where they may be insufficient

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file.ext — role in attack surface
...

## Entry Points
1. path/to/entry.ext:function_name — accepts [type of untrusted input]
...

## Data Flow
### Flow 1: [name]
1. Source: path/to/source.ext (untrusted input enters here)
2. Transform: path/to/transform.ext (data is [processed/validated/not validated])
3. Sink: path/to/sink.ext (sensitive operation: [db query/file write/exec/etc.])

## Dependency Chain
[Ordered list of files from entry to sink]

## Analysis
[Detailed security analysis including:
- Vulnerability class (injection, auth bypass, SSRF, etc.)
- Existing mitigations and their gaps
- Attack scenarios
- Recommended remediation]

## Summary
[Concise description of the vulnerability and its impact]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Attack surface coverage: Did you identify all files in the SASL authentication data flow?
- Entry point identification: Did you find the correct entry points (channel builders, authenticators)?
- Data flow completeness: Did you trace the full path from connection to authorized principal?
- Analysis quality: Is the SASL mechanism architecture correctly described?

71-assistanttext-
The analysis has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here is a summary of what was found:

## Key Findings

### Architecture Traced
The SASL authentication flow proceeds through these layers:
1. `ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()` → selects `SaslChannelBuilder` for SASL_PLAINTEXT/SASL_SSL
2. `SaslChannelBuilder.configure()` → creates per-mechanism callback handlers and login subjects
3. `SaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()` → wraps socket in `KafkaChannel` with lazy `SaslServerAuthenticator`
4. `SaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate()` → state machine gates all requests until auth is complete
5. State transitions: `INITIAL_REQUEST` → `HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST` → `AUTHENTICATE` → `COMPLETE`

### Entry Points Identified
- Raw TCP bytes enter at `SaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate()` (line 264)
- Mechanism name string arrives in `SaslHandshakeRequest` (validated via server-configured whitelist)
- PLAIN: NUL-delimited `authzid\0username\0password` bytes reach `PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()`
- SCRAM: Two-round structured messages parsed via strict regex in `ScramMessages.java`
- OAUTHBEARER: Raw JWT bearer token in `OAuthBearerSaslServer.evaluateResponse()`

### Critical Security Gap
The default `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` (automatically used when OAUTHBEARER is enabled without explicit handler configuration) performs **no JWT signature verification**. An attacker can craft an unsigned JWT with any `sub` claim and authenticate as any principal — a complete authentication bypass.

### Other Gaps
- PLAIN credentials transmitted in cleartext over SASL_PLAINTEXT (no enforcement of SSL requirement)
- Partial username oracle for SCRAM: unknown users fail at round 1 (before proof exchange), known users with wrong passwords fail at round 2 (ti
... (truncated)

ApiVersions\n111:         HANDSHAKE_REQUEST,             // After an ApiVersions request, next request must be SaslHandshake\n112:         AUTHENTICATE,                  // Authentication tokens re-authentication requested with wrong mechanism, generate exception\n117:     }\n118: \n119:     private final SecurityProtocol securityProtocol;\n120:     private final ListenerName      }\n217:     }\n218: \n219:     private SaslServer createSaslKerberosServer(final AuthenticateCallbackHandler saslServerCallbackHandler, final Map<String, ?> configs, Subject subject) throws IOException {\n220:         // server is using a JAAS-authenticated subject: determine service principal name and hostname from kafka server's subject.\n221:         final String servicePrincipal = Evaluates client responses via `SaslServer.evaluateResponse` and returns the issued challenge to the client until\n243:      * authentication succeeds or fails.\n244:      *\n245:      * The messages are sent and received as size delimited bytes that consists of a 4 byte network-ordered size N\n246:      * followed by N bytes representing the opaque payload.\n247:      */\n248:     @SuppressWarnings(\"fallthrough\")\n249:     @Override\n250:     public void authenticate() throws IOException {\n251:         if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\n252: (netInBuffer == null) netInBuffer = new NetworkReceive(saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize, connectionId);\n262: \n263:             try {\n264:                 netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer);\n265:             } catch (InvalidReceiveException e) {\n266:                 throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Failing SASL authentication due to invalid receive size\", e);\n267:             }\n268:             if (!netInBuffer.complete())\n269:                 return;\n270:             netInBuffer.payload().rewind();\n271:         }\n272:         byte[] clientToken = new byte[netInBuffer.payload().remaining()];\n273:         netInBuffer.payload().get(clientToken, 0, clientToken.length);\n274:         netInBuffer = null; // reset the networkReceive as we read all the data.\n275:         try {\n276:             switch (saslState) {\n277:                 case REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE:\n278:                 case HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST:\n279: Current SASL state will be updated when outgoing writes to the client complete.\n289:                     if (saslServer.isComplete())\n290:                         setSaslState(SaslState.COMPLETE);\n291:                     break;\n292:                 default:\n293:                     break;\n294:             }\n295:         } catch (AuthenticationException e) {\n296:             // Exception will be propagated after response is sent to client\n297:             setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, e);\n298:         } catch (Exception e) {\n299:             // In the case of IOExceptions and other unexpected exceptions, fail immediately\n300:             saslState = SaslState.FAILED;\n301:             LOG.debug(\"Failed during {}: {}\", reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText(), e.getMessage());\n302:             throw e;\n303:         }\n304:     }\n305: \n306:     @Override\n307:     public KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n308:         Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n309:                 Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n310:         SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol,\n311:                 clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n312:         KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n313:         if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) && Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n314:             principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n315:         }\n316:         return principal;\n317:     }\n318: \n319:     @Override\n320:     public Optional<KafkaPrincipalSerde> principalSerde() {\n321:         return principalBuilder instanceof KafkaPrincipalSerde ? \n334:     @Override\n335:     public void close() throws IOException {\n336:         if (principalBuilder instanceof Closeable)\n337:             Utils.closeQuietly((Closeable) principalBuilder, @Override\n360:     public Long serverSessionExpirationTimeNanos() {\n361:         return reauthInfo.sessionExpirationTimeNanos;\n362:     }\n363: \n364:     @Override\n365:     public Long      return flushedCompletely;\n401:     }\n402: \n403:     private boolean flushNetOutBuffer() throws IOException {\n404:         if (!netOutBuffer.completed())\n405: }\n420: \n421:     private void handleSaslToken(byte[] clientToken) throws IOException {\n422:         if (!enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders) {\n423:             byte[] response = ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(clientToken);\n435:             RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n436:             ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n437:             RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n438:                     KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n439:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n440:             if (apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_AUTHENTICATE) {\n441:                 IllegalSaslStateException e = new IllegalSaslStateException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL authentication.\");\n442:                 buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, requestAndSize.request.getErrorResponse(e));\n443:                 throw e;\n444:             }\n445:             short version = header.apiVersion();\n446:             if (!header.isApiVersionSupported()) {\n447:                 // We cannot create an error response if the request version of SaslAuthenticate is not supported\n448:                 // This should not normally occur since clients typically check supported versions using ApiVersionsRequest\n449:                 throw new UnsupportedVersionException(\"Version \" + version + \" is not supported for apiKey \" + apiKey);\n450:             }\n451:             /*\n452:              * The client sends multiple SASL_AUTHENTICATE requests, and the client is known\n453:              * to support the required version if any one of them indicates it supports that\n454:              * version.\n455:              */\n456:             if (!reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication)\n457:                 reauthInfo.connectedClientSupportsReauthentication = version > 0;\n458:                      .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n479:                                 .setErrorMessage(e.getMessage())));\n480:                 throw e;\n481:                  // Handle retriable Kerberos exceptions as I/O exceptions rather than authentication exceptions\n485:                     throw e;\n486:                 } else {\n487:                     // DO NOT include error message from the `SaslException` in the client response since it may\n488:                     // contain sensitive data like the existence of the user.\n489:                     String errorMessage = \"Authentication failed during \"\n490:                             + reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText()\n491:                             + \" due to invalid credentials with SASL mechanism \" + saslMechanism;\n492:                     buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n493:                             new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n494:                             .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n495:                             .setErrorMessage(errorMessage)));\n496:                     throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage, e);\n497:                 }\n498:             }\n499:         }\n500:     }\n501: \n502:     /**\n503:      * @throws InvalidRequestException if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid. Clients\n504:      * that support SASL without support for KIP-43 (e.g. Kafka Clients 0.9.x) are in the former bucket - the first\n505:      * packet such clients send is a GSSAPI token starting with 0x60.\n506:      */\n507:     private void handleKafkaRequest(byte[] requestBytes) throws IOException, AuthenticationException {\n508:         try {\n509:             ByteBuffer requestBuffer = ByteBuffer.wrap(requestBytes);\n510:             RequestHeader header = RequestHeader.parse(requestBuffer);\n511:             ApiKeys apiKey = header.apiKey();\n512: \n513:             // Raise an error prior to parsing if the api cannot be handled at this layer. This avoids\n514:             // unnecessary exposure to some of the more complex schema types.\n515:             if (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n516:                 throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n517: \n518:             LOG.debug(\"Handling Kafka request {} during {}\", apiKey, reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText());\n519: \n520:             RequestContext requestContext = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, clientAddress(), Optional.of(clientPort()),\n521:                     KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\n522:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = requestContext.parseRequest(requestBuffer);\n523: \n524:             // A valid Kafka request was received, we can now update the sasl state\n525:             if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST)\n526:                 setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST);\n527: \n528:             if (apiKey == ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS)\n529:                 handleApiVersionsRequest(requestContext, (ApiVersionsRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n530:             else {\n531:                 String clientMechanism = handleHandshakeRequest(requestContext, (SaslHandshakeRequest) requestAndSize.request);\n532:                 if (!reauthInfo.reauthenticating() || reauthInfo.saslMechanismUnchanged(clientMechanism)) {\n533:                     createSaslServer(clientMechanism);\n534:                     setSaslState(SaslState.AUTHENTICATE);\n535:                 }\n536:             }\n537:         } catch (InvalidRequestException e) {\n538:             if (saslState == SaslState.INITIAL_REQUEST) {\n539:                 // InvalidRequestException is thrown if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid.\n540:                 // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\n541:                 // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\n542:                 throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with the \" +\n543:                     \"wrong security protocol, it does not support KIP-43 or it is not a kafka client.\", e);\n544:             }\n545:             throw e;\n546:         }\n547:     }\n548: \n549:     private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\n550:         String clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();\n551:         short version = context.header.apiVersion();\n552:         if (version >= 1)\n553:             this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(true);\n554:         if (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\n555:             LOG.debug(\"Using SASL mechanism '{}' provided by client\", clientMechanism);\n556:             sendKafkaResponse(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n557:                     new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.NONE.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n558:             return clientMechanism;\n559:         } else {\n560:             LOG.debug(\"SASL mechanism '{}' requested by client is not supported\", clientMechanism);\n561:             buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(context, new SaslHandshakeResponse(\n562:                     new SaslHandshakeResponseData().setErrorCode(Errors.UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM.code()).setMechanisms(enabledMechanisms)));\n563:             throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n564:         }\n565:     }\n566: \n567:     // Visible to override for testing\n568:     protected void enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders(boolean flag) {\n569:         this.enableKafkaSaslAuthenticateHeaders = flag;\n570:     }\n571: \n572:     private void handleApiVersionsRequest(RequestContext context, ApiVersionsRequest apiVersionsRequest) throws IOException {\n573:         if (saslState != SaslState.HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST)\n574:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"Unexpected ApiVersions request received during SASL authentication state \" + saslState);\n575: \n576:         if (apiVersionsRequest.hasUnsupportedRequestVersion())\n577:             sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.UNSUPPORTED_VERSION.exception()));\n578:         else if (!apiVersionsRequest.isValid())\n579:             sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionsRequest.getErrorResponse(0, Errors.INVALID_REQUEST.exception()));\n580:         else {\n581:             metadataRegistry.registerClientInformation(new ClientInformation(apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareName(),\n582:                 apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareVersion()));\n583:             sendKafkaResponse(context, apiVersionSupplier.apply(apiVersionsRequest.version()));\n584:             setSaslState(SaslState.HANDSHAKE_REQUEST);\n585:         }\n586:     }\n587: \n588:     /**\n589:      * Build a {@link Send} response on {@link #authenticate()} failure. The actual response is sent out when\n590:      * {@link #sendAuthenticationFailureResponse()} is called.\n591:      */\n592:     private void buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(RequestContext context, AbstractResponse response) {\n593:         authenticationFailureSend = context.buildResponseSend(response);\n594:     }\n595: \n596:     /**\n597:      * Send any authentication failure response that may have been previously built.\n598:      */\n599:     private void sendAuthenticationFailureResponse() throws IOException {\n600:         if (authenticationFailureSend == null)\n601:             return;\n602:         sendKafkaResponse(authenticationFailureSend);\n603:         authenticationFailureSend = null;\n604:     }\n605: \n606:     private void sendKafkaResponse(RequestContext   "content": "# Kafka SASL Authentication Flow Security Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java` \u2014 Factory for all channel builders; selects SASL/SSL/Plaintext based on `SecurityProtocol`; constructs `SaslChannelBuilder` with per-mechanism JAAS contexts\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java` \u2014 Wires up per-mechanism callback handlers (`PlainServerCallbackHandler`, `ScramServerCallbackHandler`, `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, `SaslServerCallbackHandler`); creates `SaslServerAuthenticator` via supplier lazy-evaluated on first connection\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java` \u2014 Represents a single connection; delegates authentication to an `Authenticator` instance; calls `authenticate()` until `complete()` returns true before accepting normal requests\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java` \u2014 Core server-side SASL state machine; reads raw bytes from transport layer; dispatches to `handleKafkaRequest()` or `handleSaslToken()` based on state; enforces receive-size limit (default 512 KB)\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslClientAuthenticator.java` \u2014 Client-side SASL authenticator; sends ApiVersionsRequest, SaslHandshakeRequest, and mechanism-specific tokens\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java` \u2014 PLAIN mechanism server; parses NUL-delimited `[authzid]\\0authcid\\0passwd` message; delegates credential check to callback handler\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` \u2014 Validates PLAIN credentials against JAAS config entries (`user_<username>` keys) using timing-safe comparison\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java` \u2014 SCRAM-SHA-256/512 server; two-round challenge-response; nonce verification; cryptographic proof via HMAC; timing-safe stored-key comparison\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java` \u2014 Looks up SCRAM credentials from in-memory `CredentialCache` (populated from ZooKeeper/KRaft); also handles delegation token lookup\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMessages.java` \u2014 Parses SCRAM protocol messages using strict regex patterns; raises `SaslException` on format violations\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java` \u2014 OAUTHBEARER server; parses bearer token from client response; calls callback handler for JWT validation; uses `OAuthBearerToken.principalName()` as authorization ID\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/unsecured/OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java` \u2014 **Development-only** default OAuthBearer validator; validates only `exp`/`nbf`/`iat` timing claims; performs NO cryptographic signature verification; used automatically unless a production handler is explicitly configured\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java` \u2014 Extracts `KafkaPrincipal` from `SaslAuthenticationContext` using `SaslServer.getAuthorizationID()`; applies `KerberosShortNamer` for GSSAPI\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/KafkaPrincipal.java` \u2014 Identity object used throughout authorization; carries `principalType` (\"User\") and `name` (the authenticated identity); also tracks `tokenAuthenticated` flag\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/authorizer/Authorizer.java` \u2014 Pluggable ACL authorization interface; `authorize(requestContext, actions)` called per-request after authentication completes\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java` \u2014 Loads JAAS login module configuration; supports both static file-based and dynamic `sasl.jaas.config` property; blocks disallowed login modules\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java` \u2014 In-memory store for SCRAM credentials per mechanism; populated by AdminClient operations via ZooKeeper/KRaft metadata\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n1. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 250) \u2014 accepts raw bytes from any TCP client connecting on a SASL listener; no authentication required at this point\n2. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleKafkaRequest()` (line 507) \u2014 parses untrusted bytes as Kafka request headers (`ApiVersionsRequest` or `SaslHandshakeRequest`); mechanism name string comes from client\n3. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (line 421) \u2014 accepts raw bytes for mechanism-specific SASL token exchange; routes to `SaslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken)` without intermediate sanitization\n4. `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 71) \u2014 accepts NUL-delimited bytes containing authzid, username, and plaintext password from the untrusted client\n5. `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 96) \u2014 accepts two rounds of client-supplied SCRAM protocol bytes (`ClientFirstMessage` with username+nonce, `ClientFinalMessage` with proof)\n6. `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 86) \u2014 accepts raw OAuth bearer token bytes from client; parses token value and authorizationId\n7. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleHandshakeRequest()` (line 549) \u2014 reads client-supplied mechanism name string; validates against server-configured whitelist\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Flow 1: PLAIN Authentication (credential in cleartext token)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 264) \u2014 `netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer)` reads raw TCP bytes up to `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` (default 524,288 bytes)\n2. **Transform**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (line 461) \u2014 bytes passed directly to `saslServer.evaluateResponse(Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()))` with no intermediate validation\n3. **Transform**: `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 85-89) \u2014 raw bytes decoded as UTF-8, split on NUL (`\\u0000`) into `[authzid, username, password]` tokens; empty username/password rejected (lines 91-96)\n4. **Callback**: `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java:authenticate()` (line 61-69) \u2014 constructs JAAS key `\"user_\" + username` and looks up expected password; comparison via `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` (timing-safe)\n5. **Sink**: `PlainSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` (line 137) returns `authorizationId = username` \u2192 `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()` creates `KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", username)` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()` enforces ACLs\n\n### Flow 2: SCRAM-SHA-256 Authentication (multi-round challenge-response)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 264) \u2014 reads raw bytes from transport layer per round\n2. **Round 1 \u2013 ClientFirstMessage**: `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 100) \u2014 `new ClientFirstMessage(response)` parses bytes using regex `PATTERN` in `ScramMessages.java` (line 68-74); extracts `saslName`, `nonce`, optional `authorizationId`, and extensions; username resolved via `ScramFormatter.username(saslName)`\n3. **Credential Lookup**: `ScramServerCallbackHandler.java:handle()` (line 66-67) \u2014 `credentialCache.get(username)` fetches stored `ScramCredential` (salt, iterations, storedKey, serverKey); null credential \u2192 authentication fails\n4. **Server Response**: `ScramSaslServer.java` (line 135-138) \u2014 sends `ServerFirstMessage` with combined nonce (client nonce + server nonce), salt, and iteration count back to client\n5. **Round 2 \u2013 ClientFinalMessage**: `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 149) \u2014 parses `ClientFinalMessage`; verifies nonce matches (line 150-151); calls `verifyClientProof()` (line 153)\n6. **Proof Verification**: `ScramSaslServer.java:verifyClientProof()` (line 227-236) \u2014 `MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey)` (timing-safe); `InvalidKeyException` on HMAC failure\n7. **Sink**: `ScramSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` returns `authorizationId = username` \u2192 `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()` \u2192 `KafkaPrincipal` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()`\n\n### Flow 3: OAUTHBEARER Authentication (JWT bearer token)\n\n1. **Source**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 95) \u2014 `new OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse(response)` parses client-supplied bytes; extracts `tokenValue`, `authorizationId`, and SASL extensions\n2. **Transform**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:process()` \u2014 calls `callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{validatorCallback, extensionsCallback})`\n3. **Default validation** (dev-only): `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` \u2014 decodes JWT without signature verification; checks `exp`/`nbf`/`iat` timestamps only; extracts principal name from a configurable claim (`sub` by default)\n4. **Sink**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` (line 108) returns `tokenForNegotiatedProperty.principalName()` \u2014 value comes entirely from client-supplied JWT payload \u2192 `KafkaPrincipal` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()`\n\n### Flow 4: Mechanism Negotiation (SaslHandshake)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleKafkaRequest()` (line 509) \u2014 raw bytes parsed as `RequestHeader` then `SaslHandshakeRequest`\n2. **Transform**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleHandshakeRequest()` (line 550) \u2014 `clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism()` reads mechanism string from untrusted client\n3. **Validation**: `enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)` (line 554) \u2014 whitelist check against server-configured mechanisms; unsupported mechanisms return `UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM` error\n4. **Decision**: if valid, `createSaslServer(clientMechanism)` (line 533) \u2014 creates the mechanism-specific `SaslServer` instance; state transitions to `AUTHENTICATE`\n\n### Flow 5: Principal to ACL Authorization\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:principal()` (line 307) \u2014 called after `saslServer.isComplete()` is true\n2. **Transform**: `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java:build()` (line 80-84) \u2014 creates `KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", saslServer.getAuthorizationID())`; for GSSAPI, applies `KerberosShortNamer` rules\n3. **Sink**: `Authorizer.java:authorize(requestContext, actions)` \u2014 receives `requestContext.principal()` which is the `KafkaPrincipal`; matches against ACL bindings by principal type + name + host + operation + resource\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n```\nTCP connection accepted on SASL listener\n  \u2502\n mechanism\n  \u2502  creates per-mechanism AuthenticateCallbackHandler\n  \u2502  acquires LoginManager / Subject\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nSaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()\n  \u2502  wraps SocketChannel in TransportLayer (Plaintext or SSL)\n  \u2502  creates KafkaChannel with lazy SaslServerAuthenticator supplier\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nSaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate()   \u2190 raw bytes enter here\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500[INITIAL_REQUEST / HANDSHAKE states]\u2500\u2500\u25bahandleKafkaRequest()\n  \u2502                                          \u2502\n  \u2502 rejected\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Architecture Summary\n\nThe Kafka SASL subsystem uses a layered architecture:\n\n1. **Channel layer** (`ChannelBuilders` \u2192 `SaslChannelBuilder`): Configures the security protocol and creates per-mechanism infrastructure from broker configuration (JAAS, callback handlers, login subjects).\n2. **Authentication layer** (`SaslServerAuthenticator`): Implements a strict state machine that gates all protocol access. Until authentication is `COMPLETE`, no normal Kafka API requests are processed.\n3. **Mechanism layer** (`PlainSaslServer`, `ScramSaslServer`, `OAuthBearerSaslServer`, GSSAPI): Pluggable implementations via `javax.security.sasl.SaslServer` interface; each receives raw bytes and is responsible for its own protocol parsing and credential verification.\n4. **Callback layer** (`PlainServerCallbackHandler`, `ScramServerCallbackHandler`): Decouples credential storage from protocol logic, enabling custom credential backends.\n5. **Principal/Authorization layer** (`DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder` \u2192 `Authorizer`): Converts authenticated identity to a principal and enforces ACL-based access control.\n\n---\n\n### Vulnerability Class: Insufficient Input Validation at Mechanism Boundary\n\n**Severity: Informational to Medium (context-dependent)**\n\nAll untrusted data ultimately enters `SaslServer.evaluateResponse(byte[])`. The mechanism implementations perform their own parsing:\n- PLAIN: UTF-8 decode + NUL-character split (no length limits per field, only aggregate 512 KB limit)\n- SCRAM: Regex-validated structured message (well-defined grammar via `ScramMessages.java`)\n- OAUTHBEARER: `OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse` parses a structured message format\n\nNo cross-mechanism validation is done before dispatch; the state machine trusts that once `createSaslServer(mechanism)` selects a mechanism, all subsequent bytes belong to that mechanism's protocol.\n\n---\n\n### Critical Gap: OAuthBearer Default Handler (CVE-class: Authentication Bypass)\n\n**Severity: Critical in OAuthBearer deployments without explicit handler configuration**\n\n`SaslChannelBuilder.createServerCallbackHandlers()` (line 330-331):\n```java\nelse if (mechanism.equals(OAuthBearerLoginModule.OAUTHBEARER_MECHANISM))\n    callbackHandler = new OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler();\n```\n\nWhen `OAUTHBEARER` is in `sasl.enabled.mechanisms` but no `sasl.oauthbearer.jwks.endpoint.url` or custom `sasl.server.callback.handler.class` is configured, the broker silently uses `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`. This handler:\n- Does **not** verify JWT signatures (no HMAC or RSA/EC public key validation)\n- Accepts any well-formed JWT where `exp` is in the future\n- Extracts the principal name from the `sub` claim (or configurable claim) in the **client-supplied** JWT payload\n\n**Attack scenario**: An unauthenticated attacker can craft an arbitrary JWT with `exp` set to the future and any desired `sub` claim value (e.g., `\"admin\"` or any super-user name), base64-encode it with no signature, and authenticate as any principal. This bypasses all SASL authentication.\n\n**Existing mitigation**: The documentation (`OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java`, lines 79-80) states it \"is not suitable for production use.\" However, this is only a documentation warning; the code does not prevent use in production or emit a broker startup warning.\n\n**Recommended remediation**:\n- Emit a `WARN` log at broker startup if `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` is active\n- Consider refusing to start if `OAUTHBEARER` is enabled without a production-grade callback handler\n- Document mandatory configuration of `sasl.oauthbearer.jwks.endpoint.url` for OAUTHBEARER in all deployment guides\n\n---\n\n### Gap: PLAIN Mechanism Over Unencrypted Transport\n\n**Severity: High in SASL_PLAINTEXT deployments**\n\n`PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` transmits the password in cleartext as part of the SASL token. When used with `SASL_PLAINTEXT` (not `SASL_SSL`), these credentials traverse the network unencrypted.\n\nThe code does not enforce that PLAIN is only used over TLS. The `PlainSaslServer` does not inspect the `SecurityProtocol` or transport-layer encryption state.\n\n**Attack scenario**: A network eavesdropper on a SASL_PLAINTEXT listener can capture any connection establishment and extract plaintext credentials from the SASL token.\n\n**Existing mitigations**: Kafka documentation recommends using `SASL_SSL` for production. The separation of `SASL_PLAINTEXT` and `SASL_SSL` security protocols is enforced at the `ChannelBuilders` level.\n\n**Recommended remediation**: Add a broker startup check that rejects `PLAIN` mechanism configuration on `SASL_PLAINTEXT` listeners, or log a prominent warning.\n\n---\n\n### Gap: ClientInformation Stored Pre-Authentication (Minor Information Leak)\n\n**Severity: Low**\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.handleApiVersionsRequest()` (line 581-582):\n```java\nmetadataRegistry.registerClientInformation(new ClientInformation(\n    apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareName(),\n    apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareVersion()));\n```\n\nThe `ApiVersionsRequest` is processed **before** authentication completes, and the client-supplied `clientSoftwareName` and `clientSoftwareVersion` strings are stored in `ChannelMetadataRegistry`. These values are unauthenticated and could contain arbitrary strings from an attacker.\n\n**Attack scenario**: If `ClientInformation` is exposed in metrics, logs, or admin APIs, an attacker can inject arbitrary strings for tracking/confusion purposes. This is not an authentication bypass but affects observability integrity.\n\n---\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n| Control | Location | Effectiveness |\n|---|---|---|\n| Receive size limit (512 KB default) | `SaslServerAuthenticator` line 195-197 | Prevents OOM from oversized auth payloads |\n| Mechanism whitelist | `handleHandshakeRequest()` line 554 | Prevents use of server-unsupported mechanisms |\n| Timing-safe password comparison | `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` line 68 | Prevents timing-based username enumeration for PLAIN |\n| Timing-safe SCRAM proof comparison | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 232 | Prevents timing-based secret extraction for SCRAM |\n| Error message sanitization | `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` line 487-496 | Prevents leaking backend error details (SaslException vs SaslAuthenticationException distinction) |\n| SCRAM minimum iterations check | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 133-134 | Enforces minimum work factor |\n| Re-authentication principal check | `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` line 427, 463-464 | Prevents session hijacking during re-auth |\n| Nonce freshness check (SCRAM) | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 150-151 | Prevents replay attacks |\n| JAAS login module blocklist | `JaasContext.java` line 100 | Blocks dangerous login modules |\n| Mechanism-mechanism isolation | State machine in `SaslServerAuthenticator` | One mechanism per connection; no cross-mechanism interference |\n\n---\n\n### Attack Scenarios Summary\n\n**Scenario 1 \u2013 OAuthBearer Bypass (Critical)**\n- Precondition: Broker configured with `OAUTHBEARER` in `sasl.enabled.mechanisms`, no custom callback handler\n- Steps: Client crafts JWT `{\"alg\":\"none\"}{\"sub\":\"admin\",\"exp\":<future>}`, base64-encodes with empty signature, sends as OAUTHBEARER token\n- Result: Authenticates as principal `User:admin`; full ACL access if admin ACLs exist or no ACLs are configured\n\n**Scenario 2 \u2013 Credential Eavesdropping (PLAIN + SASL_PLAINTEXT)**\n- Precondition: Broker using SASL_PLAINTEXT with PLAIN mechanism (common in internal/development clusters)\n- Steps: Attacker with network access captures TCP stream during client authentication\n- Result: Obtains plaintext username and password directly from the SASL token\n\n**Scenario 3 \u2013 Username Enumeration via SCRAM (Mitigated but partial)**\n- Precondition: SCRAM enabled, attacker can observe authentication response timing\n- Steps: Send ClientFirstMessage for valid vs. invalid usernames\n- Partially mitigated: Null credential returns `SaslException` with generic message; BUT the `ScramServerCallbackHandler` returns null from `credentialCache.get(username)` which may have subtly different timing than a found credential (cache miss vs. hit). The timing-safe comparison is only invoked in `verifyClientProof()` during round 2, which is never reached for unknown users.\n- Result: Potential username oracle via timing difference between unknown (fails in round 1) vs. known (proceeds to round 2) users\n\n**Scenario 4 \u2013 SASL State Machine Confusion**\n- Precondition: Attacker sends unexpected API key during AUTHENTICATE state\n- Behavior: `handleSaslToken()` line 440-443 returns an error response for non-`SASL_AUTHENTICATE` API keys; throws `IllegalSaslStateException` which transitions to `FAILED` state\n- Result: Connection terminated; no authentication bypass; well-handled\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka SASL authentication subsystem implements a sound architectural foundation: a strict state machine gates all requests until authentication completes, mechanism dispatch uses a server-side whitelist, and credential verification uses timing-safe comparisons. However, two significant gaps exist in the current implementation.\n\n**The most critical issue** is the default use of `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` for OAUTHBEARER deployments without explicit production configuration. This handler performs no JWT signature verification, allowing any attacker to craft a token claiming any principal identity and authenticate without valid credentials. A broker can be silently misconfigured into this vulnerable state simply by enabling OAUTHBEARER without specifying a production callback handler.\n\n**The second significant issue** is the absence of enforcement preventing PLAIN authentication over unencrypted `SASL_PLAINTEXT` transport, exposing credentials to network eavesdroppers in misconfigured deployments.\n\nThe SCRAM implementation is cryptographically sound (HMAC-SHA-256/512, timing-safe comparison, nonce-based replay protection, minimum iteration enforcement), but introduces a partial username oracle due to authentication failing at round 1 for unknown users versus round 2 for known users with incorrect passwords.\n\nThe full path from untrusted input to authorized principal is:\n`TCP socket bytes \u2192 NetworkReceive \u2192 SaslServerAuthenticator \u2192 SaslServer.evaluateResponse() \u2192 [mechanism parsing + callback handler credential lookup] \u2192 SaslServer.getAuthorizationID() \u2192 DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder \u2192 KafkaPrincipal \u2192 Authorizer.authorize()`\n",

`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java` \u2014 OAUTHBEARER server; parses bearer token from client response; calls callback handler `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java` \u2014 Extracts `KafkaPrincipal` from `SaslAuthenticationContext` using authorization; carries `principalType` (\"User\") and `name` (the authenticated identity); also tracks `tokenAuthenticated` flag\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/authorizer/Authorizer.java` \u2014 Pluggable ACL authorization interface; `authorize(requestContext, actions)` called per-request after authentication completes\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/JaasContext.java` \u2014 Loads JAAS login module configuration; supports both static file-based and dynamic `sasl.jaas.config` property; blocks disallowed login modules\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/CredentialCache.java` \u2014 In-memory store for SCRAM credentials per mechanism; populated by AdminClient operations via ZooKeeper/KRaft metadata\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n1. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 250) \u2014 accepts raw bytes from any TCP client connecting on a SASL listener; no authentication required at this point\n2. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleKafkaRequest()` (line 507) \u2014 parses untrusted bytes as Kafka request headers (`ApiVersionsRequest` or `SaslHandshakeRequest`); mechanism name string comes from client\n3. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (line 421) \u2014 accepts raw bytes for mechanism-specific SASL token exchange; routes to `SaslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken)` without intermediate sanitization\n4. `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 71) \u2014 accepts NUL-delimited bytes containing authzid, username, and plaintext password from the untrusted client\n5. `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 96) \u2014 accepts two rounds of client-supplied SCRAM protocol bytes (`ClientFirstMessage` with username+nonce, `ClientFinalMessage` with proof)\n6. `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 86) \u2014 accepts raw OAuth bearer token bytes from client; parses token value and authorizationId\n7. `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleHandshakeRequest()` (line 549) \u2014 reads client-supplied mechanism name string; validates against server-configured whitelist\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Flow 1: PLAIN Authentication (credential in cleartext token)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 264) \u2014 `netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer)` reads raw TCP bytes up to `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` (default 524,288 bytes)\n2. **Transform**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (line 461) \u2014 bytes passed directly to `saslServer.evaluateResponse(Utils.copyArray(saslAuthenticateRequest.data().authBytes()))` with no intermediate validation\n3. **Transform**: `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 85-89) \u2014 raw bytes decoded as UTF-8, split on NUL (`\\u0000`) into `[authzid, username, password]` tokens; empty username/password rejected (lines 91-96)\n4. **Callback**: `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java:authenticate()` (line 61-69) \u2014 constructs JAAS key `\"user_\" + username` and looks up expected password; comparison via `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` (timing-safe)\n5. **Sink**: `PlainSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` (line 137) returns `authorizationId = username` \u2192 `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()` creates `KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", username)` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()` enforces ACLs\n\n### Flow 2: SCRAM-SHA-256 Authentication (multi-round challenge-response)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:authenticate()` (line 264) \u2014 reads raw bytes from transport layer per round\n2. **Round 1 \u2013 ClientFirstMessage**: `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 100) \u2014 `new ClientFirstMessage(response)` parses bytes using regex `PATTERN` in `ScramMessages.java` (line 68-74); extracts `saslName`, `nonce`, optional `authorizationId`, and extensions; username resolved via `ScramFormatter.username(saslName)`\n3. **Credential Lookup**: `ScramServerCallbackHandler.java:handle()` (line 66-67) \u2014 `credentialCache.get(username)` fetches stored `ScramCredential` (salt, iterations, storedKey, serverKey); null credential \u2192 authentication fails\n4. **Server Response**: `ScramSaslServer.java` (line 135-138) \u2014 sends `ServerFirstMessage` with combined nonce (client nonce + server nonce), salt, and iteration count back to client\n5. **Round 2 \u2013 ClientFinalMessage**: `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 149) \u2014 parses `ClientFinalMessage`; verifies nonce matches (line 150-151); calls `verifyClientProof()` (line 153)\n6. **Proof Verification**: `ScramSaslServer.java:verifyClientProof()` (line 227-236) \u2014 `MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey)` (timing-safe); `InvalidKeyException` on HMAC failure\n7. **Sink**: `ScramSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` returns `authorizationId = username` \u2192 `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()` \u2192 `KafkaPrincipal` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()`\n\n### Flow 3: OAUTHBEARER Authentication (JWT bearer token)\n\n1. **Source**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (line 95) \u2014 `new OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse(response)` parses client-supplied bytes; extracts `tokenValue`, `authorizationId`, and SASL extensions\n2. **Transform**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:process()` \u2014 calls `callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{validatorCallback, extensionsCallback})`\n3. **Default validation** (dev-only): `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` \u2014 decodes JWT without signature verification; checks `exp`/`nbf`/`iat` timestamps only; extracts principal name from a configurable claim (`sub` by default)\n4. **Sink**: `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:getAuthorizationID()` (line 108) returns `tokenForNegotiatedProperty.principalName()` \u2014 value comes entirely from client-supplied JWT payload \u2192 `KafkaPrincipal` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()`\n\n### Flow 4: Mechanism Negotiation (SaslHandshake)\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleKafkaRequest()` (line 509) \u2014 raw bytes parsed as `RequestHeader` then `SaslHandshakeRequest`\n2. **Transform**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleHandshakeRequest()` (line 550) \u2014 `clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism()` reads mechanism string from untrusted client\n3. **Validation**: `enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)` (line 554) \u2014 whitelist check against server-configured mechanisms; unsupported mechanisms return `UNSUPPORTED_SASL_MECHANISM` error\n4. **Decision**: if valid, `createSaslServer(clientMechanism)` (line 533) \u2014 creates the mechanism-specific `SaslServer` instance; state transitions to `AUTHENTICATE`\n\n### Flow 5: Principal to ACL Authorization\n\n1. **Source**: `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:principal()` (line 307) \u2014 called after `saslServer.isComplete()` is true\n2. **Transform**: `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java:build()` (line 80-84) \u2014 creates `KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", saslServer.getAuthorizationID())`; for GSSAPI, applies `KerberosShortNamer` rules\n3. **Sink**: `Authorizer.java:authorize(requestContext, actions)` \u2014 receives `requestContext.principal()` which is the `KafkaPrincipal`; matches against ACL bindings by principal type + name + host + operation + resource\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n```\nTCP connection accepted on SASL listener\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()\n  \u2502  selects SecurityProtocol (SASL_PLAINTEXT / SASL_SSL)\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nSaslChannelBuilder.configure()\n  \u2502  loads JaasContext per mechanism\n  \u2502  creates per-mechanism AuthenticateCallbackHandler\n  \u2502  acquires LoginManager / Subject\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nSaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()\n  \u2502  wraps SocketChannel in TransportLayer (Plaintext or SSL)\n  \u2502  creates KafkaChannel with lazy SaslServerAuthenticator supplier\n  \u2502\n  \u25bc\nSaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate()   \u2190 raw bytes enter here\n  \u2502\n  \u251c\u2500[INITIAL_REQUEST / HANDSHAKE states]\u2500\u2500\u25bahandleKafkaRequest()\n  \u2502                                          \u2502\n  \u2502                                          \u251c\u2500 ApiVersionsRequest \u2500\u2500\u25ba handleApiVersionsRequest()\n  \u2502                                          \u2502   registers ClientInformation (clientSoftwareName from client)\n  \u2502                                          \u2502\n  \u2502                                          \u2514\u2500 SaslHandshakeRequest \u2500\u2500\u25ba handleHandshakeRequest()\n  \u2502                                              mechanism whitelist check\n  \u2502                                              createSaslServer(mechanism)\n  \u2502\n           \u2502\n                                             \u2514\u2500 SaslServer.evaluateResponse(clientToken)\n                                                  \u2502\n                                                  \u251c\u2500[PLAIN]\u2500\u2500\u25ba PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()\n                                                  \u2502             UTF-8 decode + NUL split\n                                                  \u2502             PlainServerCallbackHandler \u2192 JAAS lookup\n                                                  \u2502\n                                                  \u251c\u2500[SCRAM]\u2500\u2500\u25ba ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()\n                                                  \u2502             ClientFirstMessage regex parse\n                                                  \u2502             ScramServerCallbackHandler \u2192 CredentialCache\n                                                  \u2502             ClientFinalMessage nonce+proof verify\n                                                  \u2502\n                                                  \u251c\u2500[OAUTHBEARER]\u2500\u2500\u25ba       \u2502                   OAuthBearerValidatorCallback (or Unsecured)\n                                                  \u2502\n rejected\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Architecture Summary\n\nThe Kafka SASL subsystem uses a layered architecture:\n\n1. **Channel layer** (`ChannelBuilders` \u2192 `SaslChannelBuilder`): Configures the security protocol and creates per-mechanism infrastructure from broker configuration (JAAS, callback handlers, login subjects).\n2. **Authentication layer** (`SaslServerAuthenticator`): Implements a strict state machine that gates all protocol access. Until authentication is `COMPLETE`, no normal Kafka API requests are processed.\n3. **Mechanism layer** (`PlainSaslServer`, `ScramSaslServer`, `OAuthBearerSaslServer`, GSSAPI): Pluggable implementations via `javax.security.sasl.SaslServer` interface; each receives raw bytes and is responsible for its own protocol parsing and credential verification.\n4. **Callback layer** (`PlainServerCallbackHandler`, `ScramServerCallbackHandler`): Decouples credential storage from protocol logic, enabling custom credential backends.\n5. **Principal/Authorization layer** (`DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder` \u2192 `Authorizer`): Converts authenticated identity to a principal and enforces ACL-based access control.\n\n---\n\n### Vulnerability Class: Insufficient Input Validation at Mechanism Boundary\n\n**Severity: Informational to Medium (context-dependent)**\n\nAll untrusted data ultimately enters `SaslServer.evaluateResponse(byte[])`. The mechanism implementations perform their own parsing:\n- PLAIN: UTF-8 decode + NUL-character split (no length limits per field, only aggregate 512 KB limit)\n- SCRAM: Regex-validated structured message (well-defined grammar via `ScramMessages.java`)\n- OAUTHBEARER: `OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse` parses a structured message format\n\nNo cross-mechanism validation is done before dispatch; the state machine trusts that once `createSaslServer(mechanism)` selects a mechanism, all subsequent bytes belong to that mechanism's protocol.\n\n---\n\n### Critical Gap: OAuthBearer Default Handler (CVE-class: Authentication Bypass)\n\n**Severity: Critical in OAuthBearer deployments without explicit handler configuration**\n\n`SaslChannelBuilder.createServerCallbackHandlers()` (line 330-331):\n```java\nelse if (mechanism.equals(OAuthBearerLoginModule.OAUTHBEARER_MECHANISM))\n    callbackHandler = new OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler();\n```\n\nWhen `OAUTHBEARER` is in `sasl.enabled.mechanisms` but no `sasl.oauthbearer.jwks.endpoint.url` or custom `sasl.server.callback.handler.class` is configured, the broker silently uses `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`. This handler:\n- Does **not** verify JWT signatures (no HMAC or RSA/EC public key validation)\n- Accepts any well-formed JWT where `exp` is in the future\n- Extracts the principal name from the `sub` claim (or configurable claim) in the **client-supplied** JWT payload\n\n**Attack scenario**: An unauthenticated attacker can craft an arbitrary JWT with `exp` set to the future and any desired `sub` claim value (e.g., `\"admin\"` or any super-user name), base64-encode it with no signature, and authenticate as any principal. This bypasses all SASL authentication.\n\n**Existing mitigation**: The documentation (`OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java`, lines 79-80) states it \"is not suitable for production use.\" However, this is only a documentation warning; the code does not prevent use in production or emit a broker startup warning.\n\n**Recommended remediation**:\n- Emit a `WARN` log at broker startup if `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` is active\n- Consider refusing to start if `OAUTHBEARER` is enabled without a production-grade callback handler\n- Document mandatory configuration of `sasl.oauthbearer.jwks.endpoint.url` for OAUTHBEARER in all deployment guides\n\n---\n\n### Gap: PLAIN Mechanism Over Unencrypted Transport\n\n**Severity: High in SASL_PLAINTEXT deployments**\n\n`PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` transmits the password in cleartext as part of the SASL token. When used with `SASL_PLAINTEXT` (not `SASL_SSL`), these credentials traverse the network unencrypted.\n\nThe code does not enforce that PLAIN is only used over TLS. The `PlainSaslServer` does not inspect the `SecurityProtocol` or transport-layer encryption state.\n\n**Attack scenario**: A network eavesdropper on a SASL_PLAINTEXT listener can capture any connection establishment and extract plaintext credentials from the SASL token.\n\n**Existing mitigations**: Kafka documentation recommends using `SASL_SSL` for production. The separation of `SASL_PLAINTEXT` and `SASL_SSL` security protocols is enforced at the `ChannelBuilders` level.\n\n**Recommended remediation**: Add a broker startup check that rejects `PLAIN` mechanism configuration on `SASL_PLAINTEXT` listeners, or log a prominent warning.\n\n---\n\n### Gap: ClientInformation Stored Pre-Authentication (Minor Information Leak)\n\n**Severity: Low**\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.handleApiVersionsRequest()` (line 581-582):\n```java\nmetadataRegistry.registerClientInformation(new ClientInformation(\n    apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareName(),\n    apiVersionsRequest.data().clientSoftwareVersion()));\n```\n\nThe `ApiVersionsRequest` is processed **before** authentication completes, and the client-supplied `clientSoftwareName` and `clientSoftwareVersion` strings are stored in `ChannelMetadataRegistry`. These values are unauthenticated and could contain arbitrary strings from an attacker.\n\n**Attack scenario**: If `ClientInformation` is exposed in metrics, logs, or admin APIs, an attacker can inject arbitrary strings for tracking/confusion purposes. This is not an authentication bypass but affects observability integrity.\n\n---\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n| Control | Location | Effectiveness |\n|---|---|---|\n| Receive size limit (512 KB default) | `SaslServerAuthenticator` line 195-197 | Prevents OOM from oversized auth payloads |\n| Mechanism whitelist | `handleHandshakeRequest()` line 554 | Prevents use of server-unsupported mechanisms |\n| Timing-safe password comparison | `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` line 68 | Prevents timing-based username enumeration for PLAIN |\n| Timing-safe SCRAM proof comparison | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 232 | Prevents timing-based secret extraction for SCRAM |\n| Error message sanitization | `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` line 487-496 | Prevents leaking backend error details (SaslException vs SaslAuthenticationException distinction) |\n| SCRAM minimum iterations check | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 133-134 | Enforces minimum work factor |\n| Re-authentication principal check | `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` line 427, 463-464 | Prevents session hijacking during re-auth |\n| Nonce freshness check (SCRAM) | `ScramSaslServer.java` line 150-151 | Prevents replay attacks |\n| JAAS login module blocklist | `JaasContext.java` line 100 | Blocks dangerous login modules |\n| Mechanism-mechanism isolation | State machine in `SaslServerAuthenticator` | One mechanism per connection; no cross-mechanism interference |\n\n---\n\n### Attack Scenarios Summary\n\n**Scenario 1 \u2013 OAuthBearer Bypass (Critical)**\n- Precondition: Broker configured with `OAUTHBEARER` in `sasl.enabled.mechanisms`, no custom callback handler\n- Steps: Client crafts JWT `{\"alg\":\"none\"}{\"sub\":\"admin\",\"exp\":<future>}`, base64-encodes with empty signature, sends as OAUTHBEARER token\n- Result: Authenticates as principal `User:admin`; full ACL access if admin ACLs exist or no ACLs are configured\n\n**Scenario 2 \u2013 Credential Eavesdropping (PLAIN + SASL_PLAINTEXT)**\n- Precondition: Broker using SASL_PLAINTEXT with PLAIN mechanism (common in internal/development clusters)\n- Steps: Attacker with network access captures TCP stream during client authentication\n- Result: Obtains plaintext username and password directly from the SASL token\n\n**Scenario 3 \u2013 Username Enumeration via SCRAM (Mitigated but partial)**\n- Precondition: SCRAM enabled, attacker can observe authentication response timing\n- Steps: Send ClientFirstMessage for valid vs. invalid usernames\n- Partially mitigated: Null credential returns `SaslException` with generic message; BUT the `ScramServerCallbackHandler` returns null from `credentialCache.get(username)` which may have subtly different timing than a found credential (cache miss vs. hit). The timing-safe comparison is only invoked in `verifyClientProof()` during round 2, which is never reached for unknown users.\n- Result: Potential username oracle via timing difference between unknown (fails in round 1) vs. known (proceeds to round 2) users\n\n**Scenario 4 \u2013 SASL State Machine Confusion**\n- Precondition: Attacker sends unexpected API key during AUTHENTICATE state\n- Behavior: `handleSaslToken()` line 440-443 returns an error response for non-`SASL_AUTHENTICATE` API keys; throws `IllegalSaslStateException` which transitions to `FAILED` state\n- Result: Connection terminated; no authentication bypass; well-handled\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka SASL authentication subsystem implements a sound architectural foundation: a strict state machine gates all requests until authentication completes, mechanism dispatch uses a server-side whitelist, and credential verification uses timing-safe comparisons. However, two significant gaps exist in the current implementation.\n\n**The most critical issue** is the default use of `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` for OAUTHBEARER deployments without explicit production configuration. This handler performs no JWT signature verification, allowing any attacker to craft a token claiming any principal identity and authenticate without valid credentials. A broker can be silently misconfigured into this vulnerable state simply by enabling OAUTHBEARER without specifying a production callback handler.\n\n**The second significant issue** is the absence of enforcement preventing PLAIN authentication over unencrypted `SASL_PLAINTEXT` transport, exposing credentials to network eavesdroppers in misconfigured deployments.\n\nThe SCRAM implementation is cryptographically sound (HMAC-SHA-256/512, timing-safe comparison, nonce-based replay protection, minimum iteration enforcement), but introduces a partial username oracle due to authentication failing at round 1 for unknown users versus round 2 for known users with incorrect passwords.\n\nThe full path from untrusted input to authorized principal is:\n`TCP socket bytes \u2192 NetworkReceive \u2192 SaslServerAuthenticator \u2192 SaslServer.evaluateResponse() \u2192 [mechanism parsing + callback handler credential lookup] \u2192 SaslServer.getAuthorizationID() \u2192 DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder \u2192 KafkaPrincipal \u2192 Authorizer.authorize()`\n",

# Kafka SASL Authentication Flow Security Analysis

## Files Examined

- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java` — Factory for all channel builders; selects SASL/SSL/Plaintext based on `SecurityProtocol`; constructs `SaslChannelBuilder` with per-mechanism JAAS contexts
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java` — Wires up per-mechanism callback handlers (`PlainServerCallbackHandler`, `ScramServerCallbackHandler`, `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, `SaslServerCallbackHandler`); creates `SaslServerAuthenticator` via supplier lazy-evaluated on first connection
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java` — Represents a single connection; delegates authentication to an `Authenticator` instance; calls `authenticate()` until `complete()` returns true before accepting normal requests
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java` — Core server-side SASL state machine; reads raw bytes from transport layer; dispatches to `handleKafkaRequest()` or `handleSaslToken()` based on state; enforces receive-size limit (default 512 KB)
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslClientAuthenticator.java` — Client-side SASL authenticator; sends ApiVersionsRequest, SaslHandshakeRequest, and mechanism-specific tokens
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java` — PLAIN mechanism server; parses NUL-delimited `[authzid]\0authcid\0passwd` message; delegates credential check to callback handler
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` — Validates PLAIN credentials against JAAS
